  <h3 class="timeline-comment-header-text f5 text-normal">



    <strong class="css-truncate">
      

  <a class="author link-gray-dark css-truncate-target width-fit" show_full_name="false" data-hovercard-type="user" data-hovercard-url="/users/mrc0mmand/hovercard" data-octo-click="hovercard-link-click" data-octo-dimensions="link_type:self" href="/mrc0mmand">mrc0mmand</a>

    commented


      <a href="#issuecomment-557282312" id="issuecomment-557282312-permalink" class="link-gray js-timestamp"><relative-time datetime="2019-11-21T21:34:58Z" class="no-wrap">Nov 21, 2019</relative-time></a>


    <span class="js-comment-edit-history">
    </span>
  </h3>
</div>


    <div class="edit-comment-hide js-edit-comment-hide" >

      
<task-lists disabled sortable>
<table class="d-block">
  <tbody class="d-block">
    <tr class="d-block">
      <td class="d-block comment-body markdown-body  js-comment-body">
          <p><a class="user-mention" data-hovercard-type="user" data-hovercard-url="/users/evverx/hovercard" data-octo-click="hovercard-link-click" data-octo-dimensions="link_type:self" href="https://github.com/evverx">@evverx</a> as the local fuzzer master, do you have any idea what's going on in the Azure Pipelines? The current issue is that Ubuntu Xenial (16.x) has a pretty ancient <code>libcryptsetup</code> (1.6.6) yet the current requirement has been bumped to 2.0.0 (as older <code>libcryptsetup</code> libs don't have LUKS2 support). Anyway, in Travis CI (Fuzzit stage) and the first half of the Azure Pipeline job <code>HAVE_LIBCRYPTSETUP</code> is set to <code>false</code> (even though <code>libcryptsetup</code> is installed), thus the compilation passes. However, in the second half of the Azure job <code>libcryptsetup</code> is suddenly a required dependency, thus the final error message:</p>
<pre><code>[fuzz-unit-file-build]: meson.build:996:8: ERROR: Invalid version of dependency, need 'libcryptsetup' ['&gt;= 2.0.0'] found '1.6.6'.
</code></pre>
<p>I'm not sure what causes that (maybe the clang version, which is <code>6.0.1</code> in the first half, yet <code>10.0.0</code> in the second one, or it's something completely different).</p>
<p>Also, would it be possible to bump the whole fuzzit-related infrastructure to Ubuntu Bionic (18.x)? From a quick peek at the <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/devops/pipelines/agents/hosted?view=azure-devops" rel="nofollow">Azure documentation</a> the <code>vmImage: 'ubuntu-latest'</code> directive should already point to Ubuntu 18.x, but it still uses Xenial repos, so again, I'm quite confused.</p>
      </td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
</task-lists>

Both <code>fuzzbuzz</code> and <code>infra/helper.py</code> pull Xenial images (using <code>docker</code>) to create the build environment so I don't think Ubuntu Bionic running on VMs where Xenial containers are launched would help there. I'll take a closer look later this week.</p>

      <code>
        <a title="cryptsetup: add native pkcs#11 support to cryptsetup

This adds a new crypttab option for volumes &quot;pkcs11-uri=&quot; which takes a
PKCS#11 URI. When used the key stored in the line&#39;s key file is
decrypted with the private key the PKCS#11 URI indiciates.

This means any smartcard that can store private RSA keys is usable for
unlocking LUKS devices." data-pjax="true" class="link-gray" href="/systemd/systemd/pull/14096/commits/4ffcf243b5e2ba34900bb30173f445a82322684c">cryptsetup: add native pkcs#11 support to cryptsetup</a>

    <div class="Details-content--hidden mt-2">
      <pre class="text-gray ws-pre-wrap">This adds a new crypttab option for volumes "pkcs11-uri=" which takes a

    <div class="commit-message pr-1 flex-auto min-width-0">
      <code>
        <a title="man: document new pam_systemd features in man page

This also updates the suggested PAM snippet in a number of way:

1. Be closer to the logic nowadays implemented in Fedora where the
   auth/account/password stacks are all finished off with
   pam_{deny|permit}.so

2. Make pam_unix.so just &quot;sufficient&quot; instead of &quot;required&quot; (paving
   ground for pam_systemd_home.so being hooked in as additional
   sufficient module.

3. Only do pam_nologin in the &quot;account&quot; stack, since it&#39;s about account
   validity really.

4. Use modern parameters to pam_unix when changing passwords, i.e.
   sha512 and shadow, and use already set up passwords (preparing ground
   for pam_systemd_home again)" data-pjax="true" class="link-gray" href="/systemd/systemd/pull/14096/commits/518440ea7d0958dce2b71d89fbaabfe7622d5a0d">man: document new pam_systemd features in man page</a>
      </code>

        </span>

    <div class="text-right">
      <code>
        <a href="/systemd/systemd/pull/14096/commits/518440ea7d0958dce2b71d89fbaabfe7622d5a0d" class="link-gray">518440e</a>
      </code>
    </div>
  </div>
    <div class="Details-content--hidden mt-2">
      <pre class="text-gray ws-pre-wrap">This also updates the suggested PAM snippet in a number of way:

1. Be closer to the logic nowadays implemented in Fedora where the
   auth/account/password stacks are all finished off with
   pam_{deny|permit}.so

2. Make pam_unix.so just "sufficient" instead of "required" (paving
   ground for pam_systemd_home.so being hooked in as additional
   sufficient module.

3. Only do pam_nologin in the "account" stack, since it's about account
   validity really.

4. Use modern parameters to pam_unix when changing passwords, i.e.
   sha512 and shadow, and use already set up passwords (preparing ground
   for pam_systemd_home again)</pre>
    </div>
</div>

          <strong>
              

  <a class="author link-gray-dark css-truncate-target " show_full_name="false" data-hovercard-type="user" data-hovercard-url="/users/ebiggers/hovercard" data-octo-click="hovercard-link-click" data-octo-dimensions="link_type:self" href="/ebiggers">ebiggers</a>

          <span class="text-gray">

              <a href="#discussion_r355036704" id="discussion_r355036704-permalink" class="js-timestamp link-gray d-inline-block">
                <relative-time datetime="2019-12-06T21:24:30Z" class="no-wrap">Dec 6, 2019</relative-time>
              </a>

          </span>
        </h4>

        
        
    <span class="timeline-comment-label tooltipped tooltipped-multiline tooltipped-s" aria-label="This user has previously committed to the systemd repository.">
      Contributor
    </span>





        <task-lists disabled sortable>
          <div class="comment-body markdown-body  js-comment-body">
            <p>Have you checked out the fscrypt changes in kernel v5.4?  There are new ioctls for adding/removing fscrypt keys which fix various problems with the old way, and a new encryption policy version which fixes some security limitations of the old version.  See <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.kernel.org/doc/html/latest/filesystems/fscrypt.html">https://www.kernel.org/doc/html/latest/filesystems/fscrypt.html</a></p>
<p>Since systemd-homed is new code, if you don't mind requiring kernel v5.4+ for fscrypt to be used with systemd-homed, you might want to consider supporting v2 encryption policies only.</p>
<p>Note that the other fscrypt maintainers and I aren't planning to add any new features to v1 encryption policies and the process-subscribed keyring based API for fscrypt.  They're maintained for backwards compatibility only.</p>
<p>It also looks like systemd-homed never "locks" the directory after it's been unlocked.  With the new FS_IOC_REMOVE_ENCRYPTION_KEY ioctl it would be easy to do</p>
          </div>
        </task-lists>
